<div id="review_544706782" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/544706782" />
    <a title="Marcus" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/762235-marcus"><img alt="Marcus" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593020378p2/762235.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/544706782?book_show_action=true">Feb 23, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marcus" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marcus" href="/user/show/762235-marcus">Marcus</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/762235-marcus?shelf=self-development">self-development</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/762235-marcus?shelf=eastern">eastern</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/762235-marcus?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer544706782" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5200262674052544519">The idea that I like the most from Eastern style thought is that resisting the way things are is crazy. There's a voice in my, and probably everyone else's, head that never shuts up. I'm fine with that and don't feel a huge need to silence it, but a lot of the time what it's saying (what I'm saying to myself?) is pretty dumb. <br/><br/>The voice constantly explains and reframes what I experience to make it feel safer or more comprehensible. It resists what it doesn't understand and tries to explain it awa</span>
  <span id="freeText5200262674052544519" style="display:none">The idea that I like the most from Eastern style thought is that resisting the way things are is crazy. There's a voice in my, and probably everyone else's, head that never shuts up. I'm fine with that and don't feel a huge need to silence it, but a lot of the time what it's saying (what I'm saying to myself?) is pretty dumb. <br /><br />The voice constantly explains and reframes what I experience to make it feel safer or more comprehensible. It resists what it doesn't understand and tries to explain it away or come up with elaborate justifications for why stuff doesn't fit in with The Way Things Should Be. It demands resolution to anything that doesn't fit my mental model and it creates areas in my mind that are forbidden or painful to visit then tries to push those areas away so they'll be uncovered as seldom as possible. <br /><br />All these elaborate thought tricks work sometimes, but the idea of <i>The Untethered Soul</i> (and similar books) is that the tricks are unnecessary and detrimental to finding peace. Maybe if I let the voice inside my head keep up its constant chatter, but choose to just recognize what it's saying without either rejecting it or mentally canonizing it, I can be okay with what's happening even without understanding and categorizing every bit of it.<br /><br />I feel like that way of looking at my thoughts lets me experience both negative emotions like anger and hate as well as positive emotions in a way that doesn't have side effects like anxiety or attachment. It keeps me focused on what I'm doing which results in me doing things better. It helps me deal with situations that I don't like by freeing up mental energy that would normally be spent resisting the problem and letting me instead use that energy to resolve it.<br /><br />Even though I like the idea, I still mostly don't think this way. I tell and re-tell myself the story of how things are and why they're that way and how I'm going to fix them later and forget where I am and what I'm doing. That's why I read books like this, to remind me that there is a better way.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5200262674052544519" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2251867875" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2251867875" />
    <a title="Darius Murretti" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/70432013-darius-murretti"><img alt="Darius Murretti" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506728498p2/70432013.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2251867875?book_show_action=true">Jan 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Darius Murretti" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Darius Murretti" href="/user/show/70432013-darius-murretti">Darius Murretti</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70432013-darius-murretti?shelf=audible">audible</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2251867875" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9158727629567294295">NOTE TO SELF : I own this audio books and it is extremely well done and worth listening to again and again as I do farm work as an alternative to pulp fiction <br/><br/>GOOD POINTS : <br/>1) talks about Going beyond thought to the unlimited freedom and bliss of freedom pure consciousness . <br/><br/>2) It tells us of the futility of seeking happiness in outside circumstances that we have no control over such as other peoples behavior and tells us that we can always be happy regardless of how other act towards us if we s</span>
  <span id="freeText9158727629567294295" style="display:none">NOTE TO SELF : I own this audio books and it is extremely well done and worth listening to again and again as I do farm work as an alternative to pulp fiction <br /><br />GOOD POINTS : <br />1) talks about Going beyond thought to the unlimited freedom and bliss of freedom pure consciousness . <br /><br />2) It tells us of the futility of seeking happiness in outside circumstances that we have no control over such as other peoples behavior and tells us that we can always be happy regardless of how other act towards us if we simply become aware ( aka pay attention) to the fact that we are aware of what we are feeling rather that upon the feeling itself . The science behind it is that out awareness is "soul " which is eternal , blissful etc so if instead of focusing on our pain or pleasure we focus on THAT within ourselves that is aware of the pain or pleasure then we are clinging -not to the fleeting experience but to the eternal , blissful soul - and therefore we remain eternally happy <br /><br />The bad points : <br />1) besides just telling you to pay attention to "what" is feeling the pain or pleasure rather r than the pain or pleasure itself the book does not tell you anything about how to do it <br /><br />for example it does not tell you that if you eat a vegetarian diet your load of painful karma will be much less , it does not tell you that unless you abstain from alcohol or party drugs you will be never have the clear thinking and self control to separate your consciousness from your thoughts , It does not tell you that unless you abstain from sexual thoughts and actions outside of legal marriage you will not have the strength of will to separate your conspicuousness from your outer desires and it does not give specific meditative techniques by which you can divert your focus from the feelings to the feeler .<br /><br />above all it does not mention that the only way you can stop clinging to your false identity is to cling to something vastly superior which is the LIGHT and Sound of shabd (aka The HOLY SPIRIT , THE TAO - a very sweet melodious sound and light that is always reverberating at our eyecenter but which can be contacted only by following the instructions of a perfect living master .<br /><br />So in the end this book just remains an excellently written , emphatic appeal to the soul (the real you) to not cling this small fleeting live's pains and pleasures and not stake your happiness on these but to sate your happiness on who you really are a drop of the eternal ocean of Bliss and to try to know your self and reach your ocean . But without giving any adequate instruction guidance or support in how to do so . <br /><br />This book is about what Sant Mat calls "Being a silent observer of your destiny " it theoretically discusses what "sat sangis" experience by the practice of unceasing simran which raises the consciousness above identification with the body by raising the consciousness above the body so one feels one is observing someone else talking , walking , etc and that one is different from the person one is observing . <br /><br />Maharaj Charan Singh in the book " Die to live" ( 1978) RSSB (a free PDF is here) : <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://ejcrivello.com/Books/6.%20Die">http://ejcrivello.com/Books/6.%20Die</a>%... <br /><br />says : <br /><br /><br />"177 Q. Master, when a person is unconsciously saying simran - like if you've spent two or three<br />hours saying simran and then you have your duties to perform, and you get up and you may have to<br />go to the grocery market or down the street or something, and suddenly you realize that at the back<br />of your head somewhere simran is going on automatically - is that of any real value to you, when it's<br />just going on automatically?<br />A. Sister, the stage will come when it will go on automatically. Even if you are talking to people you<br />will feel that you're doing simran; and we should get into that habit, because only then are we able to<br />concentrate at the eye center. Only that will help us to become unconscious of the world, of what is<br />going on around us. Then we will just move as actors move on a stage.<br />In this state we will feel that there is no reality. Sometimes you will be talking to a person and you<br />will feel that you are not you, someone else is walking and talking with the other person. Simran<br />helps to separate your individuality from yourself. Then the whole day you will see the world as a<br />stage, as if somebody else is acting, talking, doing a husband's duty, a wife's duty, a child's duty, and<br />you are someone different from yourself. And that helps. That is the effect of simran, and that is<br />ultimately what we want to achieve. We want to separate our real self from this world.<br />Sometimes you may feel that somebody else is sitting in meditation and you are watching somebody<br />sitting in meditation, you are separate from the person who is meditating. That feeling does come. " -DTL Q 177<br /><br /><br />(note : no book how ever well written can help us accomplish this we need a living "God Man " who can initiate us and become roommate #2 ( roomate #1 is our mind ) and we are "the Soul as long as its just us and the mind we can not succeed--we need a LIVING master to REALIZE what this book and all books on spirituality purport <br /><br />So with that clearly stated her is the review of The Untethered Soul" : <br /><br /><br />TABLE OF CONTENTS<br />Acknowledgments<br />Introduction<br />Part I: Awakening Consciousness<br />1. The Voice Inside Your Head<br />2. Your Inner Roommate<br />3. Who Are You?<br />4. The Lucid Self<br />Part II: Experiencing Energy<br />5. Infi nite Energy<br />6. The Secrets of the Spiritual Heart<br />7. Transcending the Tendency to Close<br />Part III: Freeing Yourself<br />8. Let Go Now or Fall<br />9. Removing Your Inner Thorn<br />10. Stealing Freedom for Your Soul<br />11. Pain, the Price of Freedom<br />Part IV: Going Beyond<br />12. Taking Down the Walls<br />13. Far Far Beyond<br />14. Letting Go of False Solidity<br />Part V: Living Life<br />15. The Path of Unconditional Happiness<br />16. The Spiritual Path of Non-Resistance<br />17. Contemplating Death<br />18. The Secret of the Middle Way<br />19. The Loving Eyes of God <br /><br />The Untethered Soul should become known as<br />a modern spiritual classic. Because it so directly<br />and skillfully involves the reader in a liberating process<br />of self-inquiry. <br /><br />The teaching or argument that is offered in<br />The Untethered Soul is divided into five parts. They<br />are: Awakening Consciousness, Experiencing Energy,<br />Freeing Yourself, Going Beyond, and Living Life. <br /><br />Ramana Maharshi (1879-1950), the<br />great sage from south India, is evoked as an apt instance<br />of a teacher who was known for his penetratingly direct<br />method of instruction. The Buddha and Plato, widely<br />known teaching exemplars, are also mentioned. Yoga<br />is cited in its root sense as a method for transpersonal<br />and transformative inquiry. <br /><br />A key factor in awakening is to acknowledge<br />that the model of reality that is generated by the<br />inner voice is a much reduced and impoverished one.<br />Although it can function somewhat effectively in the<br />short run as a protective strategy for generating a selfimage<br />and maintaining self-esteem, if one would step<br />back and take a look, then it soon would become clear<br />that the model cuts the world down to a size so small<br />that very little reality can get admitted, experienced,<br />contemplated, or enjoyed. When this is acknowledged<br />and then followed by an active will to disengage from attachment to the contents of the inner dialogue, thenspiritual or transpersonal growth can begin: “There is<br />nothing more important to true growth than realizing<br />that you are not the voice of the mind – you are the one<br />who hears it” (Singer, 2007, p. 10).<br /><br />: “Come to know the one who<br />watches the voice, and you will come to know one of the<br />great mysteries of creation” (Singer, 2007, p. 13)<br /><br /><br />Until you’ve watched your [inner] roommate long<br />enough to truly understand the predicament you’re<br />in, you really have no basis for practices that help you<br />deal with the mind. Once you’ve made the decision<br />to free yourself from the mental melodrama, you are<br />ready for teachings and techniques. (Singer, 2007,<br />pp. 21-22)<br /><br />The Untethered Soul<br />invites the reader into direct experience of the essential<br />self by proposing simple experiments in awareness and by<br />taking “consciousness” for its apex term: “Consciousness<br />is the highest word you will ever utter. There is nothing<br />higher or deeper than consciousness. Consciousness is<br />pure awareness” (Singer, 2007, p. 28).<br /><br />You live in the seat of consciousness. A true spiritual<br />being lives there, without effort and without intent.<br />. . . You go so deep that you realize that’s where<br />you’ve always been. At each stage of your life you<br />have seen different thoughts, emotions, and objects<br />pass before you. But you have always been the<br />conscious receiver of all that was. (p. 29)<br /><br />The Untethered Soul welcomes the reader to<br />an inner journey that starts and ends with a quiet and<br />confident awareness of being centered in a state of<br />witness consciousness. This state can be discovered or<br />recovered despite the centrifugal pull exerted by the<br />synchronization of the five physical senses with emotions<br />and thoughts. Together they de-center one’s awareness,<br />leading one to live as eccentric, neurotic, and lost:<br />“When the consciousness gets sucked in, it no longer<br />knows itself as itself. It knows itself as the objects it is<br />experiencing. In other words, you perceive yourself as<br />these objects. You think you are the sum of your learned<br />experiences.” Yet the difference between an eccentric<br />and a centered position will be evident: “When you are a<br />centered being . . . your consciousness is always aware of<br />being conscious. Your awareness of being is independent"<br />of the inner and outer objects you happen to be aware of”<br />(Singer, 2007, pp. 35-36). <br /><br />the so world can become a "problem" only when one “overlooks<br />the looker.” In The Untethered Soul we find the same<br />perennial insight about self-remembering and selfforgetfulness:<br /><br />True meditation, according to the author, is to contemplate<br />the source of consciousness. Meditation dissolves rather<br />than solves problems, or at any rate it reveals them to be<br />somewhere beside the main objective of human life and not important compared to that objective which is to free ones soul from this illusion and reunite it with the Source of all consciousness .<br /><br />Our soul is real . This world is a dream that we will wake up from at the time of our death and realize we've wasted our precious human opportunity fretting about a "dream problems " and neglecting the REAL problem of being chained to the cycle of birth and death in 8.4 million species of plants , reptiles , birds, mammals, . Human life comes only rarely and if we dont wake up and find a LIVING GOD MAN while human and carry out his teachings after being duly initiated by him we will very likely not see the human form again for aeons . <br /><br />"Our attention is so monopolized by trifles that we have no time for our most vital concerns" Sawan Singh -Spiritual Gems (free PDF available on line) <br /><br />So "The Untethered Soul" is a very fine book AS FAR AS BOOKS GO, but reading it will make little difference is one does not find a Godman , obtain initiation and practice as directed .<br /><br />4 stars - Highly recommended<br /><br />GOOD POINTS :</span>
  <a data-text-id="9158727629567294295" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer503325010" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3663507684413687470">After a friend told me Singer's book is based on a series of lectures, the overlapping nature of the chapters made sense.<br/><br/>Untethered Soul is a bit repetitive and the language is not very imaginative, but I appreciated its message: that we are not our thoughts or emotions, but rather who/what is observing them. That we can be happier (I don't know about the ecstasy Singer promises) if we stay conscious of our relationship to our thoughts/emotions, let them happen and pass through us, and move on t</span>
  <span id="freeText3663507684413687470" style="display:none">After a friend told me Singer's book is based on a series of lectures, the overlapping nature of the chapters made sense.<br /><br />Untethered Soul is a bit repetitive and the language is not very imaginative, but I appreciated its message: that we are not our thoughts or emotions, but rather who/what is observing them. That we can be happier (I don't know about the ecstasy Singer promises) if we stay conscious of our relationship to our thoughts/emotions, let them happen and pass through us, and move on to the next moment.<br /><br />I find myself hypercritical of my thoughts now: why does my mind have to narrate/comment on everything I see? Why won't my thoughts shut up? Can "I" tell them to shut up? Can't I even take a shower without my mind churning through a billion stupid, yet stress-producing things?<br /><br />Boy, is my work ever cut out for me ...</span>
  <a data-text-id="3663507684413687470" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1979746148" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18358249774501417588">I will likely be coming back to this book every year. Especially Chapter 8. The book is about mindfulness and mediation, but it's one of the most helpful ones out there because its analogies and stories are very good illustrations of complex mental processes. He does a good job of explaining what you should visualize, for example, when you try not to get caught up in your emotions. </span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('XFgWO3ktoL9MM3imMrU5YjvzWjwpPLMJQx9Yj+3AV/ooeBC7yeinBfUgPa6WztiRPs2x8Ii5aqSiVjh+ONOKXQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('UD+YBr9WUH0aogolprFkelQ7WDeQ6UOwDDj1ZHDi2fckH56GD5NXx6OxTy0CyoWJUQWz+zFsmh3tcZWVpfEEUA==')})
  }

      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_6708'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6708.The_Power_of_Now?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">The Power of Now: A Guide to Spiritual Enlightenment<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/4493.Eckhart_Tolle?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Eckhart Tolle<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p3\"><\/span><\/span> 4.13 avg rating &mdash; 214,297 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 1997\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer11381316938543490262\">Eckhart Tolle\'s message is simple: living in the now is the truest path to happiness and enlightenment. And while this message may not seem stunningly original or fresh, Tolle\'s clear writing, supportive voice and enthusiasm make this an excellent ma<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText11381316938543490262\" style=\"display:none\">Eckhart Tolle\'s message is simple: living in the now is the truest path to happiness and enlightenment. And while this message may not seem stunningly original or fresh, Tolle\'s clear writing, supportive voice and enthusiasm make this an excellent manual for anyone who\'s ever wondered what exactly &quot;living in the now&quot; means. Foremost, Tolle is a world-class teacher, able to explain complicated concepts in concrete language. More importantly, within a chapter of reading this book, readers are already holding the world in a different container--more conscious of how thoughts and emotions get in the way of their ability to live in genuine peace and happiness.Tolle packs a lot of information and inspirational ideas into The Power of Now. (Topics include the source of Chi, enlightened relationships, creative use of the mind, impermanence and the cycle of life.) Thankfully, he\'s added markers that symbolise &quot;break time&quot;. This is when readers should close the book and mull over what they just read. As a result, The Power of Now reads like the highly acclaimed A Course in Miracles--a spiritual guidebook that has the potential to inspire just as many study groups and change just as many lives for the better. --Gail Hudson<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"11381316938543490262\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n    <\/div>\n\n      <div The Seat of the Soul became a national bestseller when it was first published, but more people are buying it now than ever before. Why is this?  It is because a new species is being born. The Seat of the Soul is about this birth. This new species longs for harmony, cooperation, sharing, and reverence for Life. It uses higher orders of logic and justice -- those of the heart. I dream of a world where people respect each other and the living Earth, and spiritual growth is the first priority. I work daily to develop the awareness, compassion, and intentions that are necessary to create it. The extraordinary reception of The Seat of the Soul shows me, among other things, how many fellow souls are doing the same. <span id="freeTextContainer17816201849795540096">Michael A. Singer is the author of the highly successful The Untethered Soul, which has also been published in Turkey, Brazil (in Portuguese), Switzerland (in German), Spain, Japan, China, the Netherlands, Denmark, Finland, Poland, and Italy.<br/><br/>Singer received a master's degree in economics from the University of Florida in 1971. During his doctoral work, he had a deep inner awakening and went into s</span>
  <span id="freeText17816201849795540096" style="display:none">Michael A. Singer is the author of the highly successful The Untethered Soul, which has also been published in Turkey, Brazil (in Portuguese), Switzerland (in German), Spain, Japan, China, the Netherlands, Denmark, Finland, Poland, and Italy.<br /><br />Singer received a master's degree in economics from the University of Florida in 1971. During his doctoral work, he had a deep inner awakening and went into seclusion to focus on yoga and meditation. In 1975, he founded Temple of the Universe, a now long-established yoga and meditation center where people of any religion or set of beliefs can come together to experience inner peace. Through the years, Singer has made major contributions in the areas of business, the arts, education, healthcare, and environmental protection. He previously authored two books on the integration of Eastern and Western philosophy: The Search for Truth and Three Essays on Universal Law: Karma, Will and Love.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17816201849795540096" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
